text:
I've been looking for a good chocolate cookie base recipe and finally found it with this! I substituted the peanut butter chips for coarsley chopped Andes Mints candies (I've been looking for an excuse to use them) and they were to die for! Followed the rest of the recipe just about exactly (other than cutting back on the sugar just slightly). I baked them for 9 minutes, then finished with my "perfect cookie trick" by removing them from the oven, then dropping the pan from about 8" in the air onto the hard countertop (Seriously! Try this!), and letting them continue-cook on the hot cookie sheet for another 2 minutes before removing them to a wire rack to cool. They were crispy on the outside, moist, chewy and decadent on the inside and all-around cookie perfection! The best part of this cookie recipe is that all of the cookies turn out exactly the same size, shape and texture. These freeze beautifully in a ziplock bag to extend the "life" of that fresh-baked cookie taste, and my whole family just loved them. Just a note: Don't ruin this great cookie by using stick margarine in place of the butter (that stick margarine stuff is so hydrogenated, it's one molecule away from a plastic! lol) - much, much better with the real thing. Can't wait to try other "chips" with this recipe in the future. Thanks for the great find!

text:
This is a soft, buttery, rich chocolate cookie that I found changes dramatically depending on how it goes into the oven.  Soft, chewy, crispy, will all depend on how flat and how big the cookie dough balls are going in.  I did the first batch straight from the scoop and they turned out thick and soft.  A lot of people prefer their cookies this way so I can't downgrade them for that.  The second batch I used the same amount of dough but flattened them slightly (as I always do and should have stuck with here too!) - a little chewier, not quite as thick, and much better, at least for my tastes.  Peanut butter and chocolate fans who love soft cookies will love this one.

text:
Here's the thing--I made this recipe with my youngest boy and we lost a little flour in the process of measuring it and getting it to the mixer bowl, we lost a little egg during the egg-cracking process, and I'm not really sure if my son snuck in more sugar while I was getting my camera. With this said, even though I was sketchy about how this recipe might turn out with the little mistakes that were made, this recipe turned out a very nice cookie. Soft and fluffy and very nicely chocolate-y. (The raw batter was in-sane......but don't tell my kids that. Ha.) The best part is they did NOT stick to the pan AND I didn't need to chill the dough, which for me were excellent parts of this recipe. Next time, I'd like to try this with half of the butter replaced with peanut butter. I bet that would be really good. GREAT rainy day recipe to make with my son and bond. We had a BLAST and he was so proud of himself. NOTE: 350 for just about ten minutes was just right for us.

text:
So good!  I like this recipe a lot better than the Hershey's/Reese's recipe on this site.  I baked them at about 7.5 minutes so they are soft and chewy.  I used half whole-wheat pastry flour and Sunspire pb chips (no trans-fats).  Also used 1/2 cup brown sugar and the rest white (next time I would probably reduce the sugar by about 1/4 cup).  I got more than 2 dozen too, using my pampered chef scoop.  These cookies taste great and look beautiful too!

I looved these. Infortunately, it was not unanimous, but I still think they deserve 5 stars. I followed the recipe exactly, and the dough is quite thick and stiff. For those who like thin chewy cookies that are not too dense, this is not the cookies for you. These cookies are really heavy, thick and dense, and that is what I like about them! They do not spread much. You can feel both the flavors of the peanut and the chocolate. People all have different tastes, so I did not rate it according to whether everyone loved it or not, just rated according to whether it is a good cookie that comes out the way it says it will...and it does! Loved it, kids and brothers loved it too! thanks!!

The best cookies ever! Taking some other suggestions I made a few changed. I turned the 1 c. butter into 1/4 c. unsweetened applesauce, 1/4 c. natural pb, 1/2 c. room temp butter. Also used 1/2 c. brown sugar, 3/4 c. white sugar and special dark chocolate powder. That cuts down the sweetness so the little peanut butter nuggets really stand out. text:
This is a 5-star cookie for sure!!  I followed the recipe exactly as written except I used Reese's Pieces mini baking chips because that's what I had on hand - sooo good - these would be great for halloween cookies this way because of the colors!  The chocolate flavor of this cookie, and the texture, are PERFECT!  So many possibilties with this recipe as far as add-ins... looking forward to making this with the andes candies that another reviewer mentioned!  Also, I baked some trays where I left the cookies in mounds and baked some where I pressed them down a bit.  It didn't make too much difference, but if you prefer flatter cookies, then definitely press them down a little bit.  Either way, they taste great!!!  Also, I used a medium-sized cookie scoop and got exactly 3 dozen cookies from this recipe.  IF there happen to be any cookies that don't get eaten up while they're still fresh (and yes, I know this is a big if!), crumble up what's left and freeze them... then mix into your favorite ice cream for a treat, it's delicious!!  No good cookie should go to waste :-)  UPDATE:  I followed some of the reviewers' advice the 2nd time I made these and used 3/4 cup granulated sugar and 3/4 cup brown sugar - the cookies had an even better texture!  To get a smooth look, I rolled them into balls first and then slightly flattened them before baking.  I also used Andes mints for the second batch... a perfect mint/chocolate combination!  Love this recipe.

I made a double batch of these. since that would call for 3 cups of white sugar I substituted 1 cup of brown sugar. The cheapskate pb chip company only puts 1 & 2/3 cup of pb chips in the bag so I just used 2 bags. I think my cookie scoop is on the small side but I like it that way :) I cooked them for anywhere between 7-9 min and let them rest on the hot pan for 2 min. I ended up with 130 yummy chewy slightly crisp bottom cookies! So, so, so good!!! UPDATE: made these without any Pb chips and they are just as awesome that way too! Def my go to chocolate cookie!!

This was exactly what I was craving! I had gone to the store and purchased peanut butter chips dreaming of this type of cookie, all warm and wonderful straight out of the oven. You can tell winter has arrived, let the baking begin! I searched the different recipes and saw the submitter's comment that they are impossible to screw up which was good because while baking them, I was helping three members of my family with different school/ work projects, so screw up factor would be high! As I blended and sifted, I was shocked to realize I only had 1 1/4 cups of flour! Ugh! I said to myself, " We'll find out if they are impossible to screw up." After digging around in my cupboards, I ended up using about 1/4 cup of coconut chia granola cereal and a half a cup of Cocoa Pebbles ( gotta love Fred). Anyway, thank you thank you, thank you for submitting this recipe! Believe it or not these cookies turned out beautifully and were so delicious, it was unreal! I do cook and bake a lot and can be pretty picky about what I consider good, but if these cookies can handle my healthy cereal and the kids cereal and still turn out this phenomenal, that is saying something! The cereal actually gave them a little extra wonderfullness! Thanks again for the great recipe!

Followed the recipe and a tip from another reviewer who gave her "perfect cookie" tip...bake 9 minutes pull from oven and drop the cookie sheet from about 8 inches in the air onto the hard countertop then let the cookies cook on the hot cookie sheet for 2 minutes then transfer cookies to cooling rack. I had to make a lot of changes.  The first time around i followed the recipe exact and they came out like dry little balls.  The 2nd time around I changed it up a bit.  I used less regular sugar and added brown sugar.  I used 1 stick plus 2 tbls of butter with 1/2 cup shortening.  Used 1 cup less of flour and added 1.25 cups of instant rolled oats.  Only used 1/3 cup of cocoa.  And cut down the baking soda by 1/4 tsp and added 1/4 of baking powder. Basically a complete overhaul.  The 2nd batch came out fantastic.  The cookies spread and were chewy and moist.

Used 1/2 margarine, 1/2 Crisco...used 1/2 brown sugar, 1/2 white sugar...probably added an extra cup or so of Reese'e chips (I like my chips!).  Turned out well...first batch out of the oven was slightly underdone, so I ended up cooking the rest of them for ~12 min at 350 (they are for a bake sale, and I didn't want to risk them being underdone!).  I got 5 1/2 to 6 dozen cookies out of this batch, though!  They would have to be giant to only get 2 dozen!

text:
I made this twice. The first time around, it's way too sweet even though I use my rule of reducing sugar 25% of all the recipes here. However I really like the texture of the cookies so I played around a bit and came up with half butter/half shortening. I reduced the sugar to 3/4 cup (1/2 white and 1/4 brown). And also reduced the chips to 1 cup peanut butter chips and 1/2 cup chocolate chips to oomph the chocolate flavor. The cookies almost don't spread at all so you don't have to put it 1 inch apart. It's on the fluffy side, if you like them flatter try 1/2 tsp baking soda instead of 3/4 tsp and flatten a bit with a fork. Will definitely bake again, maybe with white chocolate chunks next time.

I like the thick and chewy nature of these cookies.  If you want a flatter cookie with the same taste, try the Reese's Chewy Chocolate Cookie recipe on this site.  I used 50%wheat and 50%white flour (adding 2-3T. of water with the wet ingredients to account for the wheat flour), and they turned out great!  Each time I make these, they get rave reviews.

text:
Scrumdiddlyumptious & very rich! Thumbs up all around at our house. The cookie is dark black & very rich (not the dark brown of brownies). I used butterscotch chips instead of peanut butter (because that is what I had) and they are delicious! This cookie goes perfect with milk or vanilla ice cream. I could see these making an outstanding ice cream-cookie sandwich.  I imagine if some wanted it to be less rich you could cut back on the cocoa. Even though these are drop cookies, I rolled them very lightly (1-2x around my palms) so they would bake evenly. Other cookies I've made w/ cocoa haven't always spread the same way as a tried & true chocolate chip cookie. They came out nice & even. The recipe made 5 dozen cookies.

This is the best cookie recipe I've ever made! I added 1 cup mini chocolate chip pieces, which went perfectly.  It was an unusually stiff dough, so, after eight minutes in the oven, I flattened them out with a fork and baked them for another five minutes. Also, instead of greasing them pan, I took the easy route and placed a piece of parchment paper on it instead. I usually double the batch, but I didn't this time, and I turned out making 24 large cookies! Tip: Eat them the morning after you've baked them with an ice-cold glass of milk for the best experience!

We loved these cookies.  What struck me is that they didn't fall flat, and were nicely soft but not mushy.  I'm glad I added almost a cup of mini semi sweet chocolate chips in addition to the other ingredients, or else I think these cookies could have turned out a bit bland.  Next time I might add a bit more salt, or use salted butter.  I also used half brown sugar and half white instead of all white sugar, in addition to being very generous with the vanilla since I didn't have a high-quality one on hand, just my emergency, better than nothing back-up generic. I kind of think those changes made it five star.

text:
ChocolatePeanutButterLover: Sub 1/3 c butter with natural peanut butter. Reduce the sugar by about 1/4 cup. Sub 1/2 white for brown sugar. 1&1/2 cups of chips is enough. Flatten dropped batter with a fork for a chewier cookie that's not as thick. Bake 9 mins. Press 1/4 c pb chips on top of the cookies right out of the oven for a nicer presentation.  XMAS: sub chips with walnut pieces and glac cherries. Makes 3 doz. btw.

text:
Amazing!!  My 7 year old daughter and I made these after school.  I prepped all the ingredients before hand to make it go smoother.  We had so much fun and I want to teach her to love to cook and make memories with the two of us sharing a special time such as making delicious cookies together.

I followed the recipe to the Tee, except for one thing....I added a secret ingredient (a tablespoon of instant decaf coffee).  I learned this trick from many pastry chefs and it truly makes a difference.  

Then, I tried the trick of baking it for 9 minutes, then taking it out of the oven and banging the cookie sheet on the counter top and letting it cook for another 2 minutes on the hot cookie sheet before taking them off. WOW, it made them crisp on the outside and soft on the inside.  

A perfect 10.  This is a keeper.  Thank you so much for sharing!

text:
Followed the recipe exactly as written, except I did not grease my pan.  I had no problems with sticking. I also cooled my cookies on cardboard; it helps to absorb some of the grease (I used to use newspaper, but I don't like newspaper ink soaking into food I'm going to feed my kids).  Cookies did not spread a lot and have a chewier texture versus crispy.  I baked mine for 10 minutes.  I got 3 dozen cookies using the Pampered Chef medium scoop.  Very simple, very good.

These cookies are very soft delicious! They have a mild chocolate taste that blends well with the peanut butter chips - I used Nestle Peanut Butter & Milk Chocolate Morsels. Also, I would recommend completely melting the butter as opposed to simply creaming it with the sugar...the dough becomes very stiff and nearly impossible to work with after you (try to) blend all the dry ingredients together. For an aesthetic touch, I rolled each cookie in sugar prior to baking it -- it came out beautiful!
